5/28/20, 10:23 AM - Jack: Check the carfax history to make sure it wasn't in a major accident, flood, or used commercially. They offering any kind of warranty? Is it certified? Do you have a friend with mechanical knowledge? Honda and Toyota I think have better used track records than Subaru.

5/28/20, 10:55 AM - John: When you ask for a quote, they will provide the state minimums for coverage based on your info. I'd recommend getting the minimum with highest deductible, except increase your liability to 100k/200k or more (this covers damage to other vehicles but also medical stuff if you injure someone), personal injury can stay low- this is for people hurt in your car which medical insurance covers unless they sue (bigger deal if you drive strangers), collision coverage should be the value of your car, finally comprehensive is not needed at all (this is for vandalism or damage to your car when you aren't driving, almost never worth the deductible)
5/28/20, 10:59 AM - Jane: Thanks!!
5/28/20, 11:02 AM - John: Your insurance premium will go up whenever there is a claim on your insurance or points on your license, and that increase means you pay back a big chunk of what was covered over time (like a weird loan), and it increases exponentially with more claims. So basically get a high deductible and plan to never use it unless absolutely necessarily.

2/21/21, 7:23 PM - John: Anole lighting fine details- make sure cage has a mesh top (not solid plastic or glass) or UVB light won't pass in. Stick all of your lights on one side of the cage so they have a temperature gradient (other side is cool and dark). Get a 2 in 1 light figure with a UVB bulb and a full spectrum incandescent heat light and put on a timer for 12-14 hours during the day, then if it drops below 70 at night I'd get a 3rd red heat light (specifically made for nocturnal reptiles) and have that turn on at night when the others are off.
2/21/21, 7:30 PM - John: Tropical hibiscus is another plant recommendation (as far as non toxic flowers go). Btw before putting plants in the terrarium, be sure to spray down the plants, rinse the pots, and maybe transplant to organic soil if you think there is any pesticides or artificial fertilBoer in there.

byÂ John O'Donohue

Nearer to the earthâ€™s heart,
Deeper within its silence:
Animals know this world
In a way we never will.
â€‹
We who are ever
Distanced and distracted
By the parade of bright
Windows thought opens:
Their seamless presence
Is not fractured thus.
â€‹
Stranded between time
Gone and time emerging,
We manage selJohn
To be where we are:
Whereas they are always
Looking out from
The here and now.
â€‹
May we learn to return
And rest in the beauty
Of animal being,
Learn to lean low,
Leave our locked minds,
And with freed senses
Feel the earth
Breathing with us.
â€‹
May we enter
Into lightness of spirit,
And slip frequently into
The feel of the wild.
â€‹
Let the clear silence
Of our animal being
Cleanse our hearts
Of corrosive words.
â€‹
May we learn to walk
Upon the earth
With all their confidence
And clear-eyed stillness
So that our minds
Might be baptBoed
In the name of the wind

And the light and the rain.

8/26/21, 1:15 PM - John: With our nanny we gave them 2 weeks paid sick leave each year,  paid federal holAbuelitays, and 1 day paid vacation accrued each month. If salaried you don't need a provision for unpaid leave, but if hourly you might want to include one (maybe 1 wk-year). Because you are a small business (under 50 employees), any additional leave (like unpaid materity), is not typical or required (in NC at least).
